**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. Remember to group similar categories together closely. Do not let similar categories stay far from each other.  Compile all your in a simple text file (step1.txt).

**Daily Briefing for Congressional Leadership**
**July 18, 2025**

**Area 1: The Epstein Controversy: Political, Legal, and Media Fallout**

**Topic 1.1: White House Response and Trump's Alleged Involvement**
The administration is engaged in a visible effort to divert public and political focus away from the Jeffrey Epstein controversy, with President Trump reportedly discussing any topic other than the files [1]. This strategy is interpreted by some media commentators as a sign of the President's "abject terror" regarding the potential contents of the unreleased documents, with his public silence on the matter cited as proof of his concern [2]. Scrutiny has been amplified by the re-emergence of a 1991 video showing President Trump at a teen modeling competition [3]. In a significant development, a report from The New Republic claims the President has deflected responsibility by implicating Attorney General Pam Bondi and FBI Director Kash Patel, alleging he "threw [them] to the wolves" on the Epstein matter [4].

**References:**
[1] Critics say Trump trying to distract from Epstein by talking about everything but that, https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/trump-steer-conversation-away-jeffrey-epstein/story?id=123927092

[2] Lawrence: Trump is living in abject terror about the Epstein files. His silence proves it., https://www.msnbc.com/the-last-word/watch/lawrence-trump-is-living-in-abject-terror-about-the-epstein-files-his-silence-proves-it-243601477897

[3] Video from 1991 shows Trump at teen modeling competition, https://www.salon.com/2025/07/21/video-from-1991-shows-trump-at-teen-modeling-competition/

[4] Trump Just Threw Pam Bondi and Kash Patel to the Wolves on Epstein, https://newrepublic.com/post/198181/donald-trump-pam-bondi-kash-patel-epstein

**Topic 1.2: Congressional Actions and Debates on File Release**
For the second consecutive week, the Epstein controversy is causing major procedural disruptions in the House of Representatives [1]. House Speaker Mike Johnson has executed a significant reversal on his previous calls for disclosure, now announcing that he is shutting down any possibility of a House vote on the files' release until at least September. The Speaker's stated rationale is that President Trump requires "space" to handle the issue [2, 3]. In a direct counter-maneuver to Democratic efforts to force a vote, House Republicans have taken the drastic step of shutting down the House floor, bringing legislative business to a "halt" specifically to prevent a vote on the Epstein matter from occurring [4].

**References:**
[1] Epstein furor upends House for second week in row, https://thehill.com/homenews/house/5412795-epstein-furor-house/

[2] Johnson Retreats on Demand for Epstein Disclosures, Saying Trump Needs ‘Space’, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/21/us/politics/mike-johnson-epstein-files-trump.html

[3] Johnson shuts door on House vote before September on releasing Epstein files, https://www.cnn.com/2025/07/21/politics/epstein-files-house-vote-gop-johnson-massie

**Topic 1.3: Media Coverage, Public Reaction, and Victim Accounts**
The public narrative is being powerfully shaped by direct accounts from Epstein's victims. One accuser, identified in reports as Maria Farmer, has described a "chilling interaction" she personally had with President Trump and has confirmed she warned law enforcement to investigate him during the initial Epstein inquiry [1]. Another victim has gone on record to directly accuse the President of lying about his involvement, stating, "He's caught" [2]. The campaign for transparency has gained a prominent voice in Martin Luther King Jr.'s daughter, who publicly challenged President Trump to "now do the Epstein files," following the administration's release of over 230,000 pages of documents pertaining to the civil rights leader [3]. Meanwhile, some media analysis questions the effectiveness of the President's deflection strategy, examining whether he is successfully "turning the tables on the Epstein story" [4].

**Area 2: Trump Administration: Domestic Policy & Governance**

**Topic 2.1: Immigration and Border Enforcement**
The administration is moving forward with concrete actions on its immigration policy. A plan is underway to expand existing military bases in New Jersey and Indiana for the purpose of detaining immigrants [1]. Separately, a new $250 "integrity fee" has been instituted for all U.S. tourist visa applicants [2]. These policies are being implemented amid sharp criticism from some publications, with headlines asserting that there is "No Safe Place for Legal Immigrants in Trump’s America" [3].

[1] Military bases in New Jersey, Indiana, to be expanded to detain immigrants, https://www.npr.org/2025/07/21/nx-s1-5475109/immigrant-detention-military-bases

**Topic 2.2: Justice Department, Law Enforcement, and Civil Rights**
Multiple developments highlight significant activity and tension involving the judiciary and federal law enforcement. The administration's use of the legal system is drawing external scrutiny, with one report noting that President Trump is leveraging the courts in a way that is "changing the shape of presidential power" [1]. This dynamic is reflected in accusations that Trump officials have defied one in three judicial rulings issued against them [2]. In a notable civil rights case, a federal judge sentenced a former police officer to nearly three years in prison for his role in the Breonna Taylor raid, a sentence that explicitly rejected the Department of Justice's recommendation for no prison time [3]. Concurrently, a federal trial is reportedly uncovering a "sprawling plan" behind the administration's actions targeting pro-Palestinian student groups [4]. At the highest level, the Supreme Court is reportedly considering a case that could lead to the overturning of a 45-year-old legal precedent [5]. Internal administration friction is also apparent, with a Trump ally publicly accusing Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell of lying under oath and recommending criminal charges [6]. Other federal actions include a raid on what was described as "California's biggest legal" marijuana farm [7].

**Topic 2.3: Social Policy and Regulations**
The administration's social policies are encountering significant legal and public challenges. A federal judge has issued an order blocking the administration's attempt to cut federal funding to Planned Parenthood [1]. In a notable policy shift, the Department of Justice has formally withdrawn its legal challenge to a Tennessee state law that prohibits the provision of gender-affirming medical care for minors [2]. The administration's ban on transgender military service remains a point of contention, with one prominent critic named McBride quoted as stating the policy "weakens our military" [3].

**Area 3: Economic & Fiscal Policy**

**Topic 3.1: Federal Budget, Deficits, and Spending**
A final fiscal analysis from the Congressional Budget Office (CBO) on a major administration legislative proposal, which headlines have dubbed "Trump's Megabill," projects a severe impact on the nation's finances. The CBO concludes the bill will directly add $3.4 trillion to the national deficit [1]. According to the same non-partisan analysis, the legislation would cause an estimated 10 million people to be kicked off their health insurance plans. In a separate analysis of a bill referred to as "Trump’s 'Big Beautiful Bill'," one report claims a specific provision allocates $300 million to be used for the protection of "the Billionaire's Properties" [2].

**Area 4: Foreign Affairs & National Security**

**Topic 4.1: Geopolitical Tensions: Russia, China, and Ukraine**
The administration's foreign policy is being linked to significant geopolitical realignments that favor U.S. adversaries. A Financial Times report, citing "western diplomats," states that a "power vacuum" left by the Trump administration at the United Nations is being aggressively exploited by China. Beijing is reportedly making a "concerted effort" to install its own officials and advance its agenda within the UN's Geneva institutions [1]. On Russia, Fiona Hill, described as a former Russia adviser to President Trump, has offered public commentary on the historical subject of why "great powers fall" [2]. Regarding the ongoing war in Ukraine, Russian President Vladimir Putin is reported to appear "unfazed" by what one headline characterizes as President Trump’s "'emotional' threats" over the conflict [3].

**Topic 4.2: Middle East Relations and Conflicts**
Reports indicate evolving dynamics and growing friction in the administration's Middle East policy. President Trump was allegedly "caught off guard" by recent Israeli military operations in both Gaza and Syria. This development is reportedly concurrent with growing skepticism toward Prime Minister Benjamin Netanyahu within the White House [1]. This situation unfolds amidst critical commentary, such as one analysis piece labeling the President's prior peacemaking promises as "naive," and arguing he is now discovering that he has been "played" [2].

**Topic 4.3: Intelligence Community and Election Security Narratives**
